## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv_dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x and time t. In nonlinear oscillator theory, the restoring force (and hence acceleration) typically depends on odd powers of displacement, possibly with damping and external driving terms dependent on time.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Cubic nonlinearity (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (Duffing oscillator restoring force)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear oscillator)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (nonlinear spring with amplitude-dependent stiffness)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) (harmonically driven linear oscillator)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Damped driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (driven Duffing with phase)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (parametrically excited oscillator)
- Van der Pol-like: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * x (nonlinear damping combined with restoring force, noting dv_dt may include velocity-dependent terms absorbed via x,t relationship)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (pendulum restoring torque as nonlinear function of angle)
- Rational restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x / (1 + c1 * x**2) (bounded nonlinear restoring force)
- Combined polynomial: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * x + c2 * x**2 + c3 * x**3 (general polynomial restoring force with asymmetry)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power polynomial restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells in nonlinear oscillators
- Sinusoidal dependence on position sin(c*x) → pendulum-type large-angle nonlinearity
- Periodic time-dependent terms cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) → external harmonic driving force
- Product of position and periodic time x*cos(c*t) → parametric excitation / modulated stiffness
- Even powers of x (x**2) in acceleration → asymmetric potential / broken symmetry in the oscillator
- Trigonometric functions of time with polynomial in x → driven nonlinear oscillator decomposition
- Acceleration depending only on x (no explicit t) → autonomous conservative or dissipative oscillator
- Nested trigonometric structure sin(c0*x + c1*t) → traveling wave or coupled phase dynamics

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:** `-1.99164100804766*x**3 - 1.99164100804766*x*(0.0248350833882069*t + 1) - 1.99164100804766*x + 0.799842060559254*sin(t)`

Let me simplify the GT:
- `-1.99164100804766*x**3` (x³ term)
- `-1.99164100804766*x*(0.0248350833882069*t + 1)` = `-1.99164100804766*x - 0.0494712882955*t*x` (linear x and t*x terms)
- `-1.99164100804766*x` (another linear x term)
- `0.799842060559254*sin(t)`

Combining: GT = `-1.99164100804766*x**3 + (-1.99164100804766 - 1.99164100804766)*x - 0.0494712882955*t*x + 0.799842060559254*sin(t)`

GT = `-1.99164100804766*x**3 - 3.98328201609532*x - 0.0494712882955*t*x + 0.799842060559254*sin(t)`

So the GT has basis functions: **x³, x, t·x, sin(t)** — that's it. No cos terms, no x² terms, no constants, no x⁵, no sin(kx), etc.

Now I'll check each candidate for whether it can reduce to exactly: `A*x³ + B*x + C*t*x + D*sin(t)`.

**Candidate 1:** `c0*cos(c1*sin(c2*t + 1)) + c3*cos(c4 + t) + x*(c5*x² + c6 + c7*t)`
The x-dependent part gives x³, x, t·x — good. But `cos(c1*sin(c2*t+1))` is a complicated time function that cannot equal a constant (unless c1=0, making it cos(0)=1, a constant). If c1=0, we get a constant term which GT doesn't have. And `c3*cos(c4+t)` = `c3*cos(c4)*cos(t) - c3*sin(c4)*sin(t)`. GT has sin(t) but no cos(t) and no constant. Setting c1=0 gives constant c0, and we need c3*cos(c4)=0 (so c3=0 or c4=π/2). If c4=π/2, then `-c3*sin(t)` matches sin(t), and c0 is a leftover constant. We can't eliminate the constant unless... wait, we could set c0=0 too. Then c1 is irrelevant. So: c0=0, c4=π/2, and the rest works. Yes!
Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `c0*cos(c1*sin(c2*t + c3)) + c4*sin(t) + x*(c5*x² + c6 + c7*t)`
